<p>The <b>Battle of Culloden</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/ən/: &#39;on&#39; in &#39;button&#39;">ən</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Scottish Gaelic</a>: <i lang="gd">Blàr Chùil Lodair</i>) was the final confrontation of the <a href="/wiki/Jacobite_rising_of_1745" title="Jacobite rising of 1745">Jacobite rising of 1745</a>. On 16 April 1746, the <a href="/wiki/Jacobitism" title="Jacobitism">Jacobite</a> forces of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Stuart" title="Charles Edward Stuart">Charles Edward Stuart</a> were decisively defeated by Hanoverian forces commanded by <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cumberland" title="Prince William, Duke of Cumberland">William Augustus, Duke of Cumberland</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Inverness" title="Inverness">Inverness</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Scottish Highlands</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Queen Anne</a>, the last monarch of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Stuart" title="House of Stuart">House of Stuart</a>, died in 1714, with no living children. Under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Settlement_1701" title="Act of Settlement 1701">Act of Settlement 1701</a>, she was succeeded by her <a href="/wiki/Second_cousin" class="mw-redirect" title="Second cousin">second cousin</a> <a href="/wiki/George_I_of_Great_Britain" title="George I of Great Britain">George I</a> of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hanover" title="House of Hanover">House of Hanover</a>, who was a descendant of the Stuarts through his maternal grandmother, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Stuart,_Queen_of_Bohemia" title="Elizabeth Stuart, Queen of Bohemia">Elizabeth</a>, a daughter of <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James VI and I</a>. The Hanoverian victory at <a href="/wiki/Culloden,_Highland" title="Culloden, Highland">Culloden</a> halted the Jacobite intent to overthrow the House of Hanover and restore the House of Stuart to the British throne; Charles Stuart never again tried to challenge Hanoverian power in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a>. The conflict was the last <a href="/wiki/Pitched_battle" title="Pitched battle">pitched battle</a> fought on British soil.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Charles Stuart's Jacobite army consisted largely of <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Episcopal_Church" title="Scottish Episcopal Church">Scottish Episcopalians</a> – mainly Scots but with a small detachment of Englishmen from the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Regiment_(Jacobite)" title="Manchester Regiment (Jacobite)">Manchester Regiment</a>. The Jacobites were supported and supplied by the <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Modern France">Kingdom of France</a> from Irish and Scots units in French service. A composite battalion of infantry ("<a href="/wiki/Irish_Picquets" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Picquets">Irish <i lang="fr" title="French language text">Picquets</i></a>"), comprising detachments from each of the regiments of the Irish Brigade plus one squadron of Irish in the French army, served at the battle alongside the regiment of Royal Scots (<i><i lang="fr" title="French language text"><a href="/wiki/Garde_%C3%89cossaise" title="Garde Écossaise">Royal Écossais</a></i></i>) raised the previous year to support the Stuart claim.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The British Government (Hanoverian loyalist) forces were mostly <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> – English, along with a significant number of Scottish Lowlanders and Highlanders, a battalion of <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulstermen</a>, some <a href="/wiki/Hessian_(soldiers)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hessian (soldiers)">Hessians</a> from Prussia,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Austrians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The quick and bloody battle on Culloden Moor was over in less than an hour, when after an unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Highland_charge" title="Highland charge">Highland charge</a> against the government lines, the Jacobites were routed and driven from the field.
</p><p>Between 1,500 and 2,000 Jacobites were killed or wounded in the brief battle.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-8587_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-8587-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-83_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-83-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In contrast, only about 300 government soldiers were killed or wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-8587_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-8587-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The battle and its aftermath continue to arouse strong feelings: the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a> awarded the Duke of Cumberland an honorary doctorate, but many modern commentators allege that the aftermath of the battle and subsequent crackdown on <a href="/wiki/Jacobitism" title="Jacobitism">Jacobitism</a> were brutal, and earned Cumberland the <a href="/wiki/Sobriquet" title="Sobriquet">sobriquet</a> "Butcher". Efforts were subsequently made to further integrate the comparatively wild <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Scottish Highlands</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>; civil penalties were introduced to weaken <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaelic culture">Gaelic culture</a> and undermine the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_clan" title="Scottish clan">Scottish clan</a> system.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(November 2010)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacobite_Standard_(1745).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Jacobite_Standard_%281745%29.svg/220px-Jacobite_Standard_%281745%29.svg.png" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Jacobite_Standard_%281745%29.svg/330px-Jacobite_Standard_%281745%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Jacobite_Standard_%281745%29.svg/440px-Jacobite_Standard_%281745%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="549" data-file-height="394" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacobite_Standard_(1745).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jacobite banner showing the Latin motto <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Tandem Triumphans</i></i>. (The motto, meaning 'At last, Triumphant', was said to have been added after the events at Glenfinnan).</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Stuart" title="Charles Edward Stuart">Charles Edward Stuart</a>, known as "Bonnie Prince Charlie" or the "Young Pretender", arrived in Scotland in 1745 to incite a rebellion of Stuart sympathizers against the House of Hanover. He successfully raised forces, mainly of <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Scottish Highland</a> <a href="/wiki/Scottish_clan" title="Scottish clan">clansmen</a>, and slipped past the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hanover" title="House of Hanover">Hanoverian</a> stationed in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and defeated a force of <a href="/wiki/Militiamen" class="mw-redirect" title="Militiamen">militiamen</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Prestonpans" title="Battle of Prestonpans">Battle of Prestonpans</a>. The city of <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> was occupied, but the castle held out and most of the Scottish population remained hostile to the rebels; others, while sympathetic, were reluctant to lend overt support to a movement whose chances were unproven. The British Government recalled forces from the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">war with France in Flanders</a> to deal with the rebellion.
</p><p>After a lengthy wait, Charles persuaded his generals that English Jacobites would stage an uprising in support of his cause. He was convinced that France would launch an invasion of England as well. His army of around 5,000 invaded England on 8 November 1745. They advanced through <a href="/wiki/Carlisle,_Cumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlisle, Cumbria">Carlisle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> to <a href="/wiki/Derby,_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Derby, England">Derby</a> and a position where they appeared to threaten <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">London</a>. It is often alleged that King <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">George II</a> made plans to decamp to <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a>, but there is no evidence for this and the King is on record as stating that he would lead the troops against the rebels himself if they approached London. (George had experience at the head of an army: in 1743 he had led his soldiers to victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dettingen" title="Battle of Dettingen">Battle of Dettingen</a>, becoming the last British monarch to lead troops into battle.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>) The Jacobites met only token resistance. There was, however, little support from English Jacobites, and the French invasion fleet was still being assembled. The armies of <a href="/wiki/Field_Marshal" class="mw-redirect" title="Field Marshal">Field Marshal</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Wade" title="George Wade">George Wade</a> and of <a href="/wiki/William_Augustus,_Duke_of_Cumberland" class="mw-redirect" title="William Augustus, Duke of Cumberland">William Augustus, Duke of Cumberland</a>, were approaching. In addition to the militia, London was defended by nearly 6,000 infantry, 700 horse and 33 artillery pieces and the Jacobites received false reports of a third army closing on them. The Jacobite general, <a href="/wiki/Lord_George_Murray_(general)" title="Lord George Murray (general)">Lord George Murray</a>, and the Council of War insisted on returning to join their growing force in Scotland. On 6 December 1745, they withdrew, with Charles Edward Stuart leaving command to Murray.
</p><p>On the long march back to Scotland, the Highland Army wore out its boots and demanded all the boots and shoes of the townspeople of <a href="/wiki/Dumfries" title="Dumfries">Dumfries</a>, as well as money and hospitality. The Jacobites reached <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> on 25 December. There they reprovisioned, having threatened to sack the city, and were joined by a few thousand additional men. They then defeated the forces of General <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hawley" title="Henry Hawley">Henry Hawley</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Falkirk_Muir" title="Battle of Falkirk Muir">Battle of Falkirk Muir</a>. The Duke of Cumberland arrived in Edinburgh on 30 January to take over command of the government army from General Hawley. He then marched north along the coast, with the army being supplied by sea. Six weeks were spent at <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a> training.
</p><p>The King's forces continued to pressure Charles. He retired north, losing men and failing to take <a href="/wiki/Stirling_Castle" title="Stirling Castle">Stirling Castle</a> or <a href="/wiki/Fort_William,_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort William, Scotland">Fort William</a>. But he invested <a href="/wiki/Fort_Augustus" title="Fort Augustus">Fort Augustus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fort_George,_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort George, Scotland">Fort George</a> in <a href="/wiki/Inverness-shire" title="Inverness-shire">Inverness-shire</a> in early April. Charles then took command again, and insisted on fighting a defensive action.
</p><p>Hugh Rose of Kilravock entertained Charles and the Duke of Cumberland respectively on 14 and 15 April 1746, before the Battle of Culloden. Charles' manners and deportment were described by his host as most engaging. Having walked out with Rose, before sitting down he watched trees being planted. He remarked, "How happy, Sir, you must feel, to be thus peaceably employed in adorning your mansion, whilst all the country round is in such commotion." Kilravock was a firm supporter of the house of Hanover, but his adherence was not solicited, nor were his preferences alluded to. The next day, the Duke of Cumberland called at the castle gate, and when Kilravock went to receive him, he bluffly observed, "So you had my cousin Charles here yesterday." Kilravock replied, "What am I to do, I am Scots", to which Cumberland replied, "You did perfectly right."
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposing_forces">Opposing forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Opposing forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jacobite_army">Jacobite army</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Jacobite army">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Highland_soldier_1744.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Highland_soldier_1744.jpg/220px-Highland_soldier_1744.jpg" width="220" height="328" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Highland_soldier_1744.jpg/330px-Highland_soldier_1744.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c3/Highland_soldier_1744.jpg 2x" data-file-width="402" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Highland_soldier_1744.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A private and corporal of a Highland regiment, circa 1744. The Highland units of the Jacobite army would have worn something very similar to the private illustrated, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Belted_plaid" title="Belted plaid">belted plaid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The Jacobite Army is often assumed to have been largely composed of Gaelic-speaking Catholic Highlanders whereas in reality some of its most effective units were recruited from the Lowlands.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> By 1745, Catholicism was confined to remote areas of the Highlands and Islands and large numbers of those who joined the Rebellion were <a href="/wiki/Nonjuring_schism" title="Nonjuring schism">Non-juring Episcopalians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Finally, while predominantly Scottish, it contained English recruits plus significant numbers of French, Scottish and Irish professionals in French service. Regardless of nationality, regulars were treated as Prisoners of War and exchanged, rather than being tried for treason. 
</p><p>One problem for the Jacobites was the difference between clan warfare, which was short-term and often based on raiding versus the professionalism and training required; even the colonels of the Macdonald regiments of Clanranald and Keppoch considered their men to be uncontrollable.<sup id="cite_ref-Harrington(2006)-35-40_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrington(2006)-35-40-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> A typical clan regiment was made up of a small minority of gentlemen (<a href="/wiki/Tacksman" title="Tacksman">tacksmen</a>) who would bear the "clan name", and under them the common soldiers or "clansmen" who bore a mixed bag of names.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid(1997)-p58_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid(1997)-p58-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The clan gentlemen formed the front ranks of the unit and were more heavily armed than their impoverished tenants who made up the bulk of the regiment.<sup id="cite_ref-Barthorp(1982)-p17-18_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barthorp(1982)-p17-18-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Because they served in the front ranks, the gentlemen suffered higher proportional casualties than the common clansman. The gentlemen of the Appin Regiment suffered one quarter of those killed, and one third of those wounded from their regiment.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid(1997)-p58_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid(1997)-p58-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The Jacobites started the campaign poorly armed; at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Prestonpans" title="Battle of Prestonpans">Prestonpans</a>, many were armed only with swords, <a href="/wiki/Lochaber_axe" title="Lochaber axe">Lochaber axes</a>, pitchforks and scythes. Although Highlanders are often pictured equipped with a broadsword, <a href="/wiki/Targe" title="Targe">targe</a> and pistol, this normally applied to only officers or gentlemen.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid(2006)-p20-22_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid(2006)-p20-22-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> After Culloden, Cumberland reported 2,320 <a href="/wiki/Firelock" class="mw-redirect" title="Firelock">firelocks</a> were recovered from the battlefield, but only 190 broadswords; this implies that of the roughly 1,000 Jacobites killed at Culloden, no more than one fifth carried a sword.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid(1997)-p50_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid(1997)-p50-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> As the campaign progressed, supplies from France improved their equipment considerably and by the time of Culloden, many were equipped with 0.69&#160;in (17.5&#160;mm) calibre French and Spanish firelocks.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid(2006)-p20-22_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid(2006)-p20-22-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the latter stage of the campaign, the Jacobites were reinforced with French regulars, many drawn from the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Brigade_(French)" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Brigade (French)">Irish Brigade in French service</a>, including Fitzjames's Horse and Irish volunteers or <i lang="fr" title="French language text"><a href="/wiki/Picket_(military)" title="Picket (military)">Picquets</a></i>. The majority of these troops were Irish born, with the exception of the <i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">Royal Écossais</i></i>, a Scottish unit in French service.<sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-4043_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-4043-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Lists of prisoners at Marshalsea, Berwick and prison interviews conducted by Captain Eyre show some were English born, claiming to have been <a href="/wiki/Impressment" title="Impressment">press-ganged</a> or seized as prisoners on British ships. Fitzjames's Horse was the only Jacobite cavalry unit to fight the whole battle on horseback.<sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-4043_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-4043-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Around 500 Irish Picquets in the French army fought in the battle, some of whom were thought to have been press-ganged from <a href="/wiki/6th_Regiment_of_Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="6th Regiment of Foot">6th (Guise's) Foot</a> taken at Fort Augustus. The <i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">Royal Écossais</i></i> also contained <a href="/wiki/Desertion" title="Desertion">deserters</a>, and the commander, Drummond, attempted to raise a second battalion after the unit had arrived in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid(2006)-p22-23_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid(2006)-p22-23-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The Jacobite artillery has been generally regarded as being ineffective in the battle. All but one of the Jacobite cannons were 3-pounders.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid(2006)-p22-23_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid(2006)-p22-23-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_army">Government army</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Government army">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:670px;max-width:670px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:142px;max-width:142px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldier_of_8th_regiment_1742.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Soldier_of_8th_regiment_1742.jpg/140px-Soldier_of_8th_regiment_1742.jpg" width="140" height="217" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Soldier_of_8th_regiment_1742.jpg/210px-Soldier_of_8th_regiment_1742.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Soldier_of_8th_regiment_1742.jpg/280px-Soldier_of_8th_regiment_1742.jpg 2x" data-file-width="390" data-file-height="604" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:142px;max-width:142px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldier_of_20th_regiment_1742.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Soldier_of_20th_regiment_1742.jpg/140px-Soldier_of_20th_regiment_1742.jpg" width="140" height="221" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Soldier_of_20th_regiment_1742.jpg/210px-Soldier_of_20th_regiment_1742.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Soldier_of_20th_regiment_1742.jpg/280px-Soldier_of_20th_regiment_1742.jpg 2x" data-file-width="383" data-file-height="604" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldier_of_34th_regiment_1742.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Soldier_of_34th_regiment_1742.jpg/120px-Soldier_of_34th_regiment_1742.jpg" width="120" height="222" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Soldier_of_34th_regiment_1742.jpg/180px-Soldier_of_34th_regiment_1742.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Soldier_of_34th_regiment_1742.jpg/240px-Soldier_of_34th_regiment_1742.jpg 2x" data-file-width="330" data-file-height="610" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldier_of_36th_regiment_1742.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Soldier_of_36th_regiment_1742.jpg/120px-Soldier_of_36th_regiment_1742.jpg" width="120" height="221" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Soldier_of_36th_regiment_1742.jpg/180px-Soldier_of_36th_regiment_1742.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Soldier_of_36th_regiment_1742.jpg/240px-Soldier_of_36th_regiment_1742.jpg 2x" data-file-width="325" data-file-height="599" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldier_of_48th_regiment_1742.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Soldier_of_48th_regiment_1742.jpg/130px-Soldier_of_48th_regiment_1742.jpg" width="130" height="227" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Soldier_of_48th_regiment_1742.jpg/195px-Soldier_of_48th_regiment_1742.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Soldier_of_48th_regiment_1742.jpg/260px-Soldier_of_48th_regiment_1742.jpg 2x" data-file-width="337" data-file-height="589" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Soldiers of the 8th, 20th,34th,36th and 48th Regiments, circa 1742</div></div></div>
<p>The Kingdom of Great Britain government army at the Battle of Culloden was made up of infantry, cavalry, and artillery. Of the army's 16 infantry battalions present, four were <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scottish</a> units and one was <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-note_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The officers of the infantry were from the upper classes and aristocracy, while the rank and file were made up of poor agricultural workers. On the outbreak of the Jacobite rising, extra incentives were given to lure recruits to fill the ranks of depleted units. For instance, on 6 September 1745, every recruit who joined the Guards before 24 September was given £6, and those who joined in the last days of the month were given £4. Regiments were named after their colonel. In theory, an infantry regiment would comprise up to ten companies of up to 70 men. They would then be 815 strong, including officers. However, regiments were rarely anywhere near this large, and at the Battle of Culloden, the regiments were not much larger than about 400 men.<sup id="cite_ref-Harrington(1991)-p25-29_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrington(1991)-p25-29-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The government cavalry arrived in Scotland in January 1746. They were not combat experienced, having spent the preceding years on anti-smuggling duties. A standard cavalryman had a Land Service pistol and a carbine. However, the main weapon used by the British cavalry was a sword with a 35-inch blade.<sup id="cite_ref-Harrington(1991)-p29-33_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrington(1991)-p29-33-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Royal Artillery vastly out-performed their Jacobite counterparts during the Battle of Culloden. However, up until this point in the campaign, the government artillery had performed dismally. The main weapon of the artillery was the 3-pounder. This weapon had a range of 500 yards (460&#160;m) and fired two kinds of shot: round iron and canister. The other weapon used was the <a href="/wiki/Coehorn_mortar" class="mw-redirect" title="Coehorn mortar">Coehorn mortar</a>. These had a calibre of &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap">4<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>2</sup>&#8260;<sub>5</sub></span> inches (11&#160;cm).<sup id="cite_ref-Harrington(1991)-p33_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrington(1991)-p33-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lead_up_to_battle">Lead up to battle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Lead up to battle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Culloden_(campaign_map_01).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Battle_of_Culloden_%28campaign_map_01%29.png/220px-Battle_of_Culloden_%28campaign_map_01%29.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Battle_of_Culloden_%28campaign_map_01%29.png/330px-Battle_of_Culloden_%28campaign_map_01%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Battle_of_Culloden_%28campaign_map_01%29.png/440px-Battle_of_Culloden_%28campaign_map_01%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Culloden_(campaign_map_01).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_Augustus_Cumberland" class="mw-redirect" title="William Augustus Cumberland">Cumberland's</a> route from <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a> towards <a href="/wiki/Culloden,_Highland" title="Culloden, Highland">Culloden</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>On 30 January, the Duke of Cumberland arrived in Scotland to take command of the government forces after the previous failures by Cope and Hawley. Cumberland decided to wait out the winter, and moved his troops northwards to <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>. Around this time, the army was increased by 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Hessian_(soldiers)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hessian (soldiers)">Hessian</a> troops. The Hessian force, led by Prince <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Landgrave_of_Hesse-Cassel" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick II, Landgrave of Hesse-Cassel">Frederick of Hesse</a>, took up position to the south to cut off any path of retreat for the Jacobites. The weather had improved to such an extent by 8 April that Cumberland again resumed the campaign. The government army reached <a href="/wiki/Cullen,_Moray" title="Cullen, Moray">Cullen</a> on 11 April, where it was joined by six battalions and two cavalry regiments.<sup id="cite_ref-PH-44_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH-44-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Days later, the government army approached the <a href="/wiki/River_Spey" title="River Spey">River Spey</a>, which was guarded by a Jacobite force of 2,000, made up of the Jacobite cavalry, the Lowland regiments and over half of the army's French regulars. The Jacobites quickly turned and fled, first towards <a href="/wiki/Elgin,_Moray" title="Elgin, Moray">Elgin</a> and then to <a href="/wiki/Nairn" title="Nairn">Nairn</a>. By 14 April, the Jacobites had evacuated Nairn, and Cumberland camped his army at Balblair just west of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-SR-5156_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR-5156-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Jacobite forces of about 5,400 left their base at <a href="/wiki/Inverness" title="Inverness">Inverness</a>, leaving most of their supplies, and assembled 5&#160;miles (8&#160;km) to the east near Drummossie,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> around 12&#160;miles (19&#160;km) before Nairn. Charles Edward Stuart had decided to personally command his forces and took the advice of his adjutant general, <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_O%27Sullivan" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir John O&#39;Sullivan">Secretary O'Sullivan</a>, who chose to stage a defensive action at Drummossie Moor,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> a stretch of open moorland enclosed between the walled <a href="/wiki/Culloden,_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Culloden, Scotland">Culloden</a><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> enclosures to the North and the walls of Culloden Park to the South.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lord_George_Murray_(general)" title="Lord George Murray (general)">Lord George Murray</a> "did not like the ground" and with other senior officers pointed out the unsuitability of the rough moorland terrain which was highly advantageous to the Duke with the <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">marshy</a> and uneven ground making the famed <a href="/wiki/Highland_charge" title="Highland charge">Highland charge</a> somewhat more difficult while remaining open to Cumberland's powerful artillery. They had argued for a guerrilla campaign, but Charles Edward Stuart refused to change his mind.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Night_attack_at_Nairn">Night attack at Nairn</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Night attack at Nairn">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 15 April, the government army celebrated Cumberland's twenty-fifth birthday by issuing two gallons of <a href="/wiki/Brandy" title="Brandy">brandy</a> to each regiment.<sup id="cite_ref-PH-44_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH-44-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> At Murray's suggestion, the Jacobites tried that evening to repeat the success of Prestonpans by carrying out a night attack on the government encampment. Murray proposed that they set off at dusk and march to <a href="/wiki/Nairn" title="Nairn">Nairn</a>. Murray planned to have the right wing of the first line attack Cumberland's rear, while Perth with the left wing would attack the government's front. In support of Perth, Charles Edward Stuart would bring up the second line. The Jacobite force however started out well after dark at about 20:00. Murray led the force cross country with the intention of avoiding government outposts. This however led to very slow going in the dark. Murray's one time <i><a href="/wiki/Aide-de-camp" title="Aide-de-camp">aide-de-camp</a></i>, James <a href="/wiki/Chevalier_de_Johnstone" title="Chevalier de Johnstone">Chevalier de Johnstone</a> later wrote, "this march across country in a dark night which did not allow us to follow any track, and accompanied with confusion and disorder".<sup id="cite_ref-SR2006-5658_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2006-5658-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> By the time the leading troop had reached Culraick, still 2 miles (3.2&#160;km) from where Murray's wing was to cross the River Nairn and encircle the town, there was only one hour left before dawn. After a heated council with other officers, Murray concluded that there was not enough time to mount a surprise attack and that the offensive should be aborted. <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_O%27Sullivan" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir John O&#39;Sullivan">O'Sullivan</a> went to inform Charles Edward Stuart of the change of plan, but missed him in the dark. Meanwhile, instead of retracing his path back, Murray led his men left, down the Inverness road. In the darkness, while Murray led one-third of the Jacobite forces back to camp, the other two-thirds continued towards their original objective, unaware of the change in plan. One account of that night even records that Perth and Drummond made contact with government troops before realising the rest of the Jacobite force had turned home. Not long after the exhausted Jacobite forces had made it back to Culloden, reports came of the advancing government troops.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2006-5658_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2006-5658-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> By then, many Jacobite soldiers had dispersed in search of food, while others were asleep in ditches and outbuildings.
</p><p>However, military historian <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Black_(historian)" title="Jeremy Black (historian)">Jeremy Black</a> has contended that even though the Jacobite force had become disordered and lost the element of surprise the night attack remained viable, and that if the Jacobites had advanced the conditions would have made government morale vulnerable and disrupted their fire discipline.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_on_Culloden_Moor">Battle on Culloden Moor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Battle on Culloden Moor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_of_the_Battle_of_Culloden.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Panorama_of_the_Battle_of_Culloden.jpg/800px-Panorama_of_the_Battle_of_Culloden.jpg" width="800" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Panorama_of_the_Battle_of_Culloden.jpg/1200px-Panorama_of_the_Battle_of_Culloden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Panorama_of_the_Battle_of_Culloden.jpg/1600px-Panorama_of_the_Battle_of_Culloden.jpg 2x" data-file-width="9971" data-file-height="1927" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_of_the_Battle_of_Culloden.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Panorama" title="Panorama">Panorama</a> of the battlefield, circa 2007. The flag on the left side indicates the Jacobite lines, the flag on the right side shows the location of the government lines.</div></div></div></div>
<p>Early on a rainy 16 April, the well-rested government army struck camp and at about 05:00 set off towards the moorland around Culloden and Drummossie. Jacobite <a href="/wiki/Picket_(military)" title="Picket (military)">pickets</a> first sighted the government <a href="/wiki/Advance_guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Advance guard">advance guard</a> at about 08:00, when the advancing army came within 4 miles (6.4&#160;km) of Drummossie. Cumberland's informers alerted him that the Jacobite army was forming up about 1 mile (1.6&#160;km) from Culloden House – upon <a href="/wiki/Culloden_Moor" class="mw-redirect" title="Culloden Moor">Culloden Moor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-47_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-47-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> At about 11:00 the two armies were within sight of one another with about 2 miles (3.2&#160;km) of open <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a> between them.<sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-47_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-47-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> As the government forces steadily advanced across the moor, the driving rain and <a href="/wiki/Rain_and_snow_mixed" title="Rain and snow mixed">sleet</a> blew from the north-east into the faces of the exhausted Jacobite army.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_moves">Opening moves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Opening moves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Jacobite army was originally arrayed between the corners of Culloden and Culwhiniac parks (from left to right): the three Macdonald battalions; a small one of <a href="/wiki/Clan_Chisholm" title="Clan Chisholm">Chisholms</a>; another small one of <a href="/wiki/Clan_Maclean" title="Clan Maclean">Macleans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clan_Maclachlan" title="Clan Maclachlan">Maclachlans</a>; Lady Mackintosh and Monaltrie's regiments; Lord Lovat's Regiment; Ardsheal's Appin Stewarts; Lochiel's Regiment; and three battalions of the Atholl Brigade. Murray who commanded the right wing, however became aware of the Leanach <a href="/wiki/Enclosure" title="Enclosure">enclosure</a> that lay ahead of him, a wall that would become an obstacle in the event of a Jacobite advance. Without any consultation he then moved the brigade down the moor and formed into three <a href="/wiki/Column_(formation)" title="Column (formation)">columns</a>. It seems probable that Murray intended to shift the axis of the Jacobite advance to a more northerly direction, thus having the right wing clear the Leanach enclosure and possibly taking advantage of the downward slope of the moor to the north.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-5868_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-5868-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, the Duke of Perth seems to have misinterpreted Murray's actions as only a general advance, and the Macdonalds on the far left simply ignored him. The result was the skewing of the Jacobite front line, with the (left wing) Macdonalds still rooted on the Culloden Parks wall and the (right wing) Atholl Brigade halfway down the Culwhiniac Parks wall. In consequence, large gaps immediately appeared in the severely over-stretched Jacobite lines. A shocked Sullivan had no choice but to position the meagre 'second line' to fill the gaps. This second line was (left to right): the Irish Picquets; the Duke of Perth's Regiment; Glenbuchat's; Lord Kilmarnock's Footguards; <a href="/wiki/John_Roy_Stuart" class="mw-redirect" title="John Roy Stuart">John Roy Stuart</a>'s Regiment; two battalions of Lord Ogilvy's Regiment; the <i>Royal Écossais</i>; two battalions of <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lewis_Gordon" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Lewis Gordon">Lord Lewis Gordon</a>'s Regiment. Farther back were cavalry units. On the left were: Lord Strathallan's Horse Bagot's <a href="/wiki/Hussars" class="mw-redirect" title="Hussars">Hussars</a> and possibly Balmerino's Lifeguards. On the right were Lord Elcho's Lifeguards and Fitzjames's Horse. And in the centre was Charles Edward Stuart's tiny <a href="/wiki/Retinue" title="Retinue">escort</a> made up of Fitzjames's Horse and Lifeguards. When Sullivan's redeployment was completed Perth's and Glenbuchat's regiments were standing on the extreme left wing and <a href="/wiki/John_Roy_Stuart" class="mw-redirect" title="John Roy Stuart">John Roy Stuart</a>'s was standing beside Ardsheal's.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-5868_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-5868-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cumberland brought forward the 13th and 62nd to extend his first and second lines. At the same time, two squadrons of Kingston's Horse were brought forward to cover the right flank. These were then joined by two troops of Cobham's 10th Dragoons. While this was taking place, Hawley began making his way through the Culwhiniac Parks intending to outflank the Jacobite right wing. Anticipating this, the two battalions of Lord Lewis Gordon's regiment had lined the wall. However, since the government dragoons stayed out of range, and the Jacobites were partly in dead ground they moved back and formed up on a <a href="/wiki/Salients,_re-entrants_and_pockets" class="mw-redirect" title="Salients, re-entrants and pockets">re-entrant</a> at Culchunaig, facing south and covering the army's rear. Once Hawley had led the dragoons through the Parks he deployed them in two lines beneath the Jacobite guarded re-entrant. By this time the Jacobites were guarding the re-entrant from above with four battalions of Lord Lewis Gordon's and Lord Ogilvy's regiments, and the combined squadron of Fitzjames's Horse and Elcho's Lifeguards. Unable to see behind the Jacobites above him, Hawley had his men stand and face the enemy.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-5868_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-5868-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Culloden_(map_02).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Battle_of_Culloden_%28map_02%29.svg/220px-Battle_of_Culloden_%28map_02%29.svg.png" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Battle_of_Culloden_%28map_02%29.svg/330px-Battle_of_Culloden_%28map_02%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Battle_of_Culloden_%28map_02%29.svg/440px-Battle_of_Culloden_%28map_02%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="774" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Culloden_(map_02).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jacobite front line skews and stretches, government forces compensate; others break into and through Culwhiniac enclosure.</div></div></div>
<p>Over the next twenty minutes, Cumberland's superior artillery battered the Jacobite lines, while Charles, moved for safety out of sight of his own forces, waited for the government forces to move. Inexplicably, he left his forces arrayed under government fire for over half an hour. Although the marshy terrain minimized casualties, the morale of the Jacobites began to suffer. Several clan leaders, angry at the lack of action, pressured Charles to issue the order to charge. The <a href="/wiki/Clan_Chattan" title="Clan Chattan">Clan Chattan</a> was first of the Jacobite army to receive this order, but an area of boggy ground in front of them forced them to veer right so that they obstructed the following regiments and the attack was pushed towards the wall. The Jacobites advanced on the left flank of the government troops, but were subjected to volleys of musket fire and the artillery which had switched from <a href="/wiki/Roundshot" class="mw-redirect" title="Roundshot">roundshot</a> to <a href="/wiki/Grapeshot" title="Grapeshot">grapeshot</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highland_charge">Highland charge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Highland charge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Culloden_Battle.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Culloden_Battle.svg/220px-Culloden_Battle.svg.png" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Culloden_Battle.svg/330px-Culloden_Battle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Culloden_Battle.svg/440px-Culloden_Battle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1052" data-file-height="744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Culloden_Battle.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jacobite front line charges the government lines.</div></div></div>
<p>Despite this many Jacobites reached the government lines and, for the first time, a battle was decided by a direct clash between <a href="/wiki/Highland_charge" title="Highland charge">charging highlanders</a> and formed redcoats equipped with muskets and socket bayonets. The brunt of the Jacobite impact was taken by just two government regiments – <a href="/wiki/4th_Regiment_of_Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="4th Regiment of Foot">Barrell's 4th Foot</a> and <a href="/wiki/37th_Regiment_of_Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="37th Regiment of Foot">Dejean's 37th Foot</a>. Barrell's regiment lost 17 and suffered 108 wounded, out of a total of 373 officers and men. Dejean's lost 14 and had 68 wounded, with this unit's left wing taking a disproportionately higher number of casualties. Barrell's regiment temporarily lost one of its two <a href="/wiki/Regimental_colours" class="mw-redirect" title="Regimental colours">colours</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;note 2&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Huske" title="John Huske">Major-General Huske</a>, who was in command of the government's second line, quickly organised the <a href="/wiki/Counter_attack" class="mw-redirect" title="Counter attack">counter attack</a>. Huske ordered forward all of Lord Sempill's Fourth Brigade which had a combined total of 1,078 men (<a href="/wiki/25th_Regiment_of_Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="25th Regiment of Foot">Sempill's 25th Foot</a>, <a href="/wiki/48th_(Northamptonshire)_Regiment_of_Foot" title="48th (Northamptonshire) Regiment of Foot">Conway's 59th Foot</a>, and <a href="/wiki/8th_Regiment_of_Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="8th Regiment of Foot">Wolfe's 8th Foot</a>). Also sent forward to plug the gap was <a href="/wiki/20th_Regiment_of_Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="20th Regiment of Foot">Bligh's 20th Foot</a>, which took up position between Sempill's 25th and Dejean's 37th. Huske's counter formed a five battalion strong <a href="/wiki/Horseshoe" title="Horseshoe">horseshoe</a>-shaped formation which <a href="/wiki/Encirclement" title="Encirclement">trapped</a> the Jacobite right wing on three sides.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Poor Barrell's regiment were sorely pressed by those desperadoes and outflanked. One stand of their <a href="/wiki/Regimental_colours" class="mw-redirect" title="Regimental colours">colours</a> was taken; Collonel Riches hand cutt off in their defence&#160;... We marched up to the enemy, and our left, <a href="/wiki/Flanking_maneuver" title="Flanking maneuver">outflanking</a> them, wheeled in upon them; the whole then gave them 5 or 6 fires with vast execution, while their front had nothing left to oppose us, but their pistolls and broadswords; and fire from their center and rear, (as, by this time, they were 20 or 30 deep) was vastly more fatal to themselves, than us.</p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite>Captain-Lieutenant James Ashe Lee of <a href="/wiki/8th_Regiment_of_Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="8th Regiment of Foot">Wolfe's 8th Foot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonet_drill_(Culloden_comparison).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Bayonet_drill_%28Culloden_comparison%29.svg/220px-Bayonet_drill_%28Culloden_comparison%29.svg.png" width="220" height="64" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Bayonet_drill_%28Culloden_comparison%29.svg/330px-Bayonet_drill_%28Culloden_comparison%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Bayonet_drill_%28Culloden_comparison%29.svg/440px-Bayonet_drill_%28Culloden_comparison%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1169" data-file-height="341" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonet_drill_(Culloden_comparison).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bayonet" title="Bayonet">Bayonet</a> drill innovation said to have been developed to counter the "<a href="/wiki/Highland_charge" title="Highland charge">Highland charge</a>". Each soldier would thrust at the enemy on his right – rather than the one straight ahead – in order to bypass the <i><a href="/wiki/Targe" title="Targe">targe</a></i> of Highlanders.<sup id="cite_ref-SR1996-Red-95658_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR1996-Red-95658-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Located on the Jacobite extreme left wing were the Macdonald regiments. Popular legend has it that these regiments refused to charge when ordered to do so, due to the perceived insult of being placed on the left wing.<sup id="cite_ref-Roberts_2002,_p._173_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts_2002,_p._173-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Even so, due to the skewing of the Jacobite front lines, the left wing had a further 200 metres (660&#160;ft) of much boggier ground to cover than the right.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;note 3&#93;</a></sup> When the Macdonalds charged, their progress was much slower than that of the rest of the Jacobite forces. Standing on the right of these regiments were the much smaller units of Chisholms and the combined unit of Macleans and Maclachlans. Every officer in the Chisholm unit was killed or wounded and Col. Lachlan Maclachlan, who led the combined unit of Macleans and Maclachlans, was gruesomely killed by a cannon shot. As the Macdonalds suffered casualties they began to give way. Immediately Cumberland then pressed the advantage, ordering two troops of <a href="/wiki/10th_Royal_Hussars" title="10th Royal Hussars">Cobham's 10th Dragoons</a> to ride them down. The boggy ground however impeded the cavalry and they turned to engage the Irish Picquets whom Sullivan had brought up in an attempt to stabilise the deteriorating Jacobite left flank.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;note 4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jacobite_collapse_and_rout">Jacobite collapse and rout</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Jacobite collapse and rout">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the collapse of the left wing, Murray brought up the <i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">Royal Écossais</i></i> and Kilmarnock's Footguards who were still at this time unengaged. However, by the time they had been brought into position, the Jacobite army was in <a href="/wiki/Rout" title="Rout">rout</a>. The <i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">Royal Écossais</i></i> exchanged musket fire with <a href="/wiki/Royal_Scots_Fusiliers" title="Royal Scots Fusiliers">Campbell's 21st</a> and commenced an orderly retreat, moving along the Culwhiniac enclosure in order to shield themselves from artillery fire. Immediately the half battalion of Highland militia commanded by Captain Colin Campbell of Ballimore which had stood inside the enclosure ambushed the <i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">Royal Écossais</i></i>. Hawley had previously left this Highland unit behind the enclosure, with orders to avoid contact with the Jacobites, to limit any chance of a <a href="/wiki/Friendly_fire" title="Friendly fire">friendly fire</a> incident. In the encounter Campbell of Ballimore was killed along with five of his men. The result was that the <i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">Royal Écossais</i></i> and Kilmarnock's Footguards were forced out into the open moor and were rushed at by three squadrons of Kerr's 11th Dragoons. The fleeing Jacobites must have put up a fight for Kerr's 11th recorded at least 16 horses killed during the entirety of the battle. The Irish picquets bravely covered the Highlanders' retreat from the battlefield and prevented a massacre. This action cost half of the 100 casualties suffered in the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The <i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">Royal Écossais</i></i> appear to have retired from the field in two wings. One part of the regiment surrendered upon the field after suffering 50 killed or wounded, but their colours were not taken and a large number retired from the field with the Jacobite Lowland regiments.<sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-8085_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-8085-48">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacobite_standard_(no9).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jacobite_standard_%28no9%29.svg/220px-Jacobite_standard_%28no9%29.svg.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jacobite_standard_%28no9%29.svg/330px-Jacobite_standard_%28no9%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jacobite_standard_%28no9%29.svg/440px-Jacobite_standard_%28no9%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacobite_standard_(no9).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of at least fourteen <a href="/wiki/Historical_colours,_standards_and_guidons" title="Historical colours, standards and guidons">standards or colours</a> recorded as captured by government forces at the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> This and a similar blue <a href="/wiki/Saltire" title="Saltire">saltire</a> may have been used by the Atholl Brigade.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>This stand by the <i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">Royal Écossais</i></i> may have given Charles Edward Stuart the time to make his escape. At the time when the Macdonald regiments were crumbling and fleeing the field, Stuart seems to have been rallying Perth's and Glenbuchat's regiments when <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_O%27Sullivan" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir John O&#39;Sullivan">O'Sullivan</a> rode up to Captain Shea who commanded Stuart's bodyguard: "Yu see all is going to pot. Yu can be of no great succor, so before a general deroute wch will soon be, Seize upon the Prince &amp; take him off&#160;...".<sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-8085_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-8085-48">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Shea then led Stuart from the field along with Perth's and Glenbuchat's regiments. From this point on the fleeing Jacobite forces were split into two groups: the Lowland regiments retired in order southwards, making their way to <a href="/wiki/Ruthven_Barracks" title="Ruthven Barracks">Ruthven Barracks</a>; the Highland regiments however were cut off by the government cavalry, and forced to retreat down the road to Inverness. The result was that they were a perfect target for the government dragoons. Major-general <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Bland" title="Humphrey Bland">Humphrey Bland</a> led the charge against the fleeing Highlanders, giving "<a href="/wiki/No_quarter" title="No quarter">Quarter to None</a> but about Fifty French Officers and Soldiers He picked up in his Pursuit".<sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-8085_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-8085-48">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conclusion:_casualties_and_prisoners">Conclusion: casualties and prisoners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Conclusion: casualties and prisoners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Jacobite <a href="/wiki/Casualty_(person)" title="Casualty (person)">casualties</a> are estimated at 1,500–2,000 killed or wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-8587_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-8587-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-83_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-83-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> As to prisoners, Lord Cumberland's official list of prisoners taken includes 154 Jacobites and 222 "French" prisoners (men from the 'foreign units' in the French service). Added to the official list of those apprehended were 172 of the Earl of Cromartie's men, captured after a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Littleferry" title="Battle of Littleferry">brief engagement the day before</a> near <a href="/wiki/Littleferry" title="Littleferry">Littleferry</a>.
</p><p>In striking contrast to the Jacobite losses, the government losses were 50 dead and 259 wounded. However, a large proportion of those recorded as wounded are likely to have died of their wounds. (For example, only 29 out of 104 wounded from Barrell's 4th Foot survived to claim pensions. All 6 of the artillerymen recorded as wounded died.)<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-8587_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-8587-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, recent geophysical studies on the government burial pit suggest the figure for deaths may have been nearer 300.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The only government casualty of high rank was <a href="/wiki/Lord_Robert_Kerr" title="Lord Robert Kerr">Lord Robert Kerr</a>, the son of <a href="/wiki/William_Kerr,_3rd_Marquess_of_Lothian" title="William Kerr, 3rd Marquess of Lothian">William Kerr, 3rd Marquess of Lothian</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%22The_End_of_the_%27Forty_Five%27_Rebellion%22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/%22The_End_of_the_%27Forty_Five%27_Rebellion%22.jpg/220px-%22The_End_of_the_%27Forty_Five%27_Rebellion%22.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/%22The_End_of_the_%27Forty_Five%27_Rebellion%22.jpg/330px-%22The_End_of_the_%27Forty_Five%27_Rebellion%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/%22The_End_of_the_%27Forty_Five%27_Rebellion%22.jpg/440px-%22The_End_of_the_%27Forty_Five%27_Rebellion%22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="433" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%22The_End_of_the_%27Forty_Five%27_Rebellion%22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The End of the 'Forty Five' Rebellion</i> depicts the retreat of the defeated <a href="/wiki/Jacobitism" title="Jacobitism">Jacobites</a>.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collapse_of_the_Jacobite_campaign">Collapse of the Jacobite campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Collapse of the Jacobite campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As the first of the fleeing Highlanders approached Inverness they were met by a battalion of <a href="/wiki/Clan_Fraser_of_Lovat" title="Clan Fraser of Lovat">Frasers</a> led by the <a href="/wiki/Simon_Fraser_of_Lovat" title="Simon Fraser of Lovat">Master of Lovat</a>. Tradition states that the Master of Lovat immediately <a href="/wiki/About-turn" class="mw-redirect" title="About-turn">about-turned</a> his men and marched down the road back towards Inverness, with pipes playing and colours flying. There are however varying traditions as to what happened at the bridge which spans the <a href="/wiki/River_Ness" title="River Ness">River Ness</a>. One tradition is that the Master of Lovat intended to hold the bridge until he was persuaded against it. Another is that the bridge was seized by a party of Argyll Militia who were involved in a skirmish when blocking the crossing of retreating Jacobites. While it is almost certain there was a skirmish upon the bridge, it has been proposed that the Master of Lovat shrewdly switched sides and turned upon the fleeing Jacobites. Such an act would explain his remarkable rise in fortune in the years that followed.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-8890_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-8890-51">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the battle, the Jacobites' Lowland units headed south, towards Corrybrough and made their way to Ruthven Barracks, while their Highland units headed north, towards Inverness and on through to Fort Augustus. There they were joined by Barisdale's Macdonalds and a small battalion of MacGregors.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-8890_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-8890-51">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The roughly 1,500 men who assembled at Ruthven Barracks received orders from Charles Edward Stuart to the effect that all was lost and to "shift for himself as best he could".<sup id="cite_ref-JLR2002-182-183_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JLR2002-182-183-52">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Similar orders must have been received by the Highland units at Fort Augustus. By 18 April the Jacobite army was disbanded. Officers and men of the units in the French service made for Inverness, where they surrendered as prisoners of war on 19 April. The rest of the army broke up, with men heading for home or attempting to escape abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-8890_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-8890-51">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Skirmish_of_Loch_nan_Uamh" title="Skirmish of Loch nan Uamh">Skirmish of Loch nan Uamh</a></div>
<p>Some ranking Jacobites made their way to <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Loch_nan_Uamh" class="mw-redirect" title="Loch nan Uamh">Loch nan Uamh</a></i>, where Charles Edward Stuart had first landed at the outset of the campaign in 1745. Here on 30 April they were met by the two French <a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigates</a> – the <i>Mars</i> and <i>Bellone</i>. Two days later the French warships were spotted and attacked by the smaller <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> <a href="/wiki/Sloops" class="mw-redirect" title="Sloops">sloops</a> – the <i><a href="/wiki/HMS_Greyhound" title="HMS Greyhound">Greyhound</a></i>, <i>Baltimore</i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/HMS_Terror" class="mw-redirect" title="HMS Terror">Terror</a></i>. The result was the last real battle in the campaign. During the six hours in which the ferocious sea-battle raged the Jacobites recovered cargo on the beach which had been landed by the French ships. In all <a href="/wiki/Pounds_sterling" class="mw-redirect" title="Pounds sterling">£</a>35,000 of gold was recovered along with supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-8890_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-8890-51">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Invigorated by the vast amounts of loot and visible proof that the French had not deserted them, the group of Highland chiefs decided to prolong the campaign. On 8 May, nearby at <a href="/wiki/Murlaggan" class="mw-redirect" title="Murlaggan">Murlaggan</a>, Lochiel, Lochgarry, Clanranald and Barisdale all agreed to rendezvous at Invermallie on 18 May. The plan was that there they would be joined by what remained of Keppoch's men and Cluny Macpherson's regiment (which did not take part in the battle at Culloden). However, things did not go as planned. After about a month of relative inactivity, Cumberland moved his regulars into the Highlands. On 17 May three battalions of regulars and eight Highland companies reoccupied Fort Augustus. The same day the Macphersons surrendered. On the day of the planned rendezvous, Clanranald never appeared and Lochgarry and Barisdale only showed up with about 300 combined (most of whom immediately dispersed in search of food). Lochiel, who commanded possibly the strongest Jacobite unit at Culloden, was only able to muster about 300. The following morning Lochiel was alerted that a body of Highlanders was approaching. Assuming they were Barisdale's Macdonalds, Locheil waited until they were identified as Loudoun's by the "red crosses in their bonnets". Locheil's men dispersed without fighting. The following week the Government launched <a href="/wiki/Raids_on_Lochaber_and_Shiramore" title="Raids on Lochaber and Shiramore">punitive expeditions into the Highlands which continued throughout the summer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-8890_51-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-8890-51">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JLR2002-182-183_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JLR2002-182-183-52">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following his flight from the battle, Charles Edward Stuart made his way towards the <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a> with some supporters. By 20 April, Stuart had reached <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Arisaig" title="Arisaig">Arisaig</a></i> on the west coast of Scotland. After spending a few days with his close associates, Stuart sailed for the island of <a href="/wiki/Benbecula" title="Benbecula">Benbecula</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a>. From there he travelled to <a href="/wiki/Scalpay,_Outer_Hebrides" title="Scalpay, Outer Hebrides">Scalpay</a>, off the east coast of <a href="/wiki/Harris_(Scotland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Harris (Scotland)">Harris</a>, and from there made his way to <a href="/wiki/Stornoway" title="Stornoway">Stornoway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-8586_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-8586-53">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> For five months Stuart criss-crossed the Hebrides, constantly pursued by government supporters and under threat from local <a href="/wiki/Laird" title="Laird">lairds</a> who were tempted to betray him for the £30,000 upon his head.<sup id="cite_ref-JP1973-301_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JP1973-301-54">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> During this time he met <a href="/wiki/Flora_MacDonald_(Scottish_Jacobite)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flora MacDonald (Scottish Jacobite)">Flora Macdonald</a>, who famously aided him in a narrow escape to <a href="/wiki/Skye" title="Skye">Skye</a>. Finally, on 19 September, Stuart reached Borrodale on <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Loch nan Uamh</i> in <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Arisaig</i>, where his party boarded two small French ships, which ferried them to France.<sup id="cite_ref-PH1991-8586_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH1991-8586-53">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> He never returned to Scotland.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Repercussions_and_persecution">Repercussions and persecution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Repercussions and persecution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:After_Culloden-_Rebel_Hunting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/After_Culloden-_Rebel_Hunting.jpg/220px-After_Culloden-_Rebel_Hunting.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/After_Culloden-_Rebel_Hunting.jpg/330px-After_Culloden-_Rebel_Hunting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/After_Culloden-_Rebel_Hunting.jpg/440px-After_Culloden-_Rebel_Hunting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="546" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:After_Culloden-_Rebel_Hunting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>After Culloden: Rebel Hunting</i> by <a href="/wiki/John_Seymour_Lucas" title="John Seymour Lucas">John Seymour Lucas</a> depicts the rigorous search for Jacobites in the days that followed Culloden.</div></div></div>
<p>The morning following the Battle of Culloden, Cumberland issued a written order reminding his men that "the public orders of the rebels yesterday was to give us no quarter".<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;note 5&#93;</a></sup> Cumberland alluded to the belief that such orders had been found upon the bodies of fallen Jacobites. In the days and weeks that followed,  versions of the alleged orders were published in the <i>Newcastle Journal</i> and the <i>Gentleman's Journal</i>. Today only one copy of the alleged order to "give no quarter" exists.<sup id="cite_ref-JR2002-177180_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JR2002-177180-57">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> It is however considered to be nothing but a poor attempt at forgery, for it is neither written nor signed by Murray, and it appears on the bottom half of a copy of a declaration published in 1745. In any event, Cumberland's order was not carried out for two days, after which contemporary accounts report then that for the next two days the moor was searched and all those wounded were put to death. On the other hand, the orders issued by Lord George Murray for the conduct of the aborted night attack in the early hours of 16 April suggest that it would have been every bit as merciless. The instructions were to use only swords, dirks and bayonets, to overturn tents, and subsequently to locate "a swelling or bulge in the fallen tent, there to strike and push vigorously".<sup id="cite_ref-JR2002-177180_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JR2002-177180-57">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;note 6&#93;</a></sup> In total, over 20,000 head of livestock, sheep, and goats were driven off and sold at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Augustus" title="Fort Augustus">Fort Augustus</a>, where the soldiers split the profits.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beheading_of_the_rebel_lords_on_great_tower_hill.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Beheading_of_the_rebel_lords_on_great_tower_hill.jpeg/220px-Beheading_of_the_rebel_lords_on_great_tower_hill.jpeg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Beheading_of_the_rebel_lords_on_great_tower_hill.jpeg/330px-Beheading_of_the_rebel_lords_on_great_tower_hill.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Beheading_of_the_rebel_lords_on_great_tower_hill.jpeg/440px-Beheading_of_the_rebel_lords_on_great_tower_hill.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1499" data-file-height="1135" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beheading_of_the_rebel_lords_on_great_tower_hill.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A contemporary <a href="/wiki/Engraving" title="Engraving">engraving</a> depicting the executions of <a href="/wiki/William_Boyd,_4th_Earl_of_Kilmarnock" title="William Boyd, 4th Earl of Kilmarnock">Kilmarnock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Elphinstone,_6th_Lord_Balmerino" title="Arthur Elphinstone, 6th Lord Balmerino">Balmerino</a> at <a href="/wiki/Tower_Hill" title="Tower Hill">Great Tower Hill</a>, on 18 August 1746<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>While in Inverness, Cumberland emptied the <a href="/wiki/Gaol" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaol">gaols</a> that were full of people imprisoned by Jacobite supporters, replacing them with Jacobites themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-8890_51-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-8890-51">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Prisoners were taken south to England to stand trial for <a href="/wiki/High_treason" title="High treason">high treason</a>. Many were held on <a href="/wiki/Prison_ship" title="Prison ship">hulks</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Thames" class="mw-redirect" title="Thames">Thames</a> or in <a href="/wiki/Tilbury_Fort" title="Tilbury Fort">Tilbury Fort</a>, and executions took place in <a href="/wiki/Carlisle,_Cumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlisle, Cumbria">Carlisle</a>, <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kennington_Park" title="Kennington Park">Kennington Common</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JP1973-301_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JP1973-301-54">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The common Jacobite supporters fared better than the ranking individuals. In total, 120 common men were executed, one third of them being deserters from the British Army.<sup id="cite_ref-JP1973-301_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JP1973-301-54">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;note 7&#93;</a></sup> The common prisoners <a href="/wiki/Sortition" title="Sortition">drew lots</a> amongst themselves and only one out of twenty actually came to trial.
