Although most of those who did stand trial were sentenced to death, almost all of these had their sentences commuted to <a href="/wiki/Penal_transportation" title="Penal transportation">penal transportation</a> to the <a href="/wiki/British_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="British colonies">British colonies</a> for life by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Traitors_Transported_Act_1746&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Traitors Transported Act 1746 (page does not exist)">Traitors Transported Act 1746</a> (20 Geo. II, c. 46).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In all, 936 men were thus transported, and 222 more were <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">banished</a>. Even so, 905 prisoners were actually released under the <a href="/wiki/Indemnity_Act_1747" class="mw-redirect" title="Indemnity Act 1747">Act of Indemnity</a> which was passed in June 1747. Another 382 obtained their freedom by being exchanged for <a href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Prisoners of war">prisoners of war</a> who were held by France. Of the total 3,471 prisoners recorded nothing is known of the fate of 648.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The high ranking "rebel lords" were executed on <a href="/wiki/Tower_Hill" title="Tower Hill">Tower Hill</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.
</p><p>Following up on the military success won by their forces, the British Government enacted laws further to integrate Scotland – specifically the Scottish Highlands – with the rest of Britain. Members of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Episcopal_Church" title="Scottish Episcopal Church">Episcopal</a> clergy were required to give oaths of allegiance to the reigning <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hanover" title="House of Hanover">Hanoverian dynasty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com-1_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-1-66">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Heritable_Jurisdictions_(Scotland)_Act_1746" title="Heritable Jurisdictions (Scotland) Act 1746">Heritable Jurisdictions (Scotland) Act 1746</a> ended the hereditary right of landowners to govern justice upon their estates through barony courts.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Previous to this act, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_feudal_barony" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish feudal barony">feudal lords</a> (which included clan chiefs) had considerable judicial and military power over their followers – such as the oft quoted power of "pit and gallows".<sup id="cite_ref-JP1973-301_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JP1973-301-54">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com-1_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-1-66">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Lords who were loyal to the Government were greatly compensated for the loss of these traditional powers, for example the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Argyll" title="Duke of Argyll">Duke of Argyll</a> was given £21,000.<sup id="cite_ref-JP1973-301_54-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JP1973-301-54">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Those lords and clan chiefs who had supported the Jacobite rebellion were stripped of their estates and these were then sold and the profits were used to further trade and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Scotland" title="Agriculture in Scotland">agriculture in Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com-1_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-1-66">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The forfeited estates were managed by <a href="/wiki/Factor_(Scotland)" title="Factor (Scotland)">factors</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dress_Act_1746" title="Dress Act 1746">Anti-clothing measures</a> were taken against the <a href="/wiki/Highland_dress" title="Highland dress">highland dress</a> by an <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament" title="Act of Parliament">Act of Parliament</a> in 1746. The result was that the wearing of <a href="/wiki/Tartan" title="Tartan">tartan</a> was banned except as a uniform for officers and soldiers in the British Army and later <a href="/wiki/Landed_gentry" title="Landed gentry">landed men</a> and their sons.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culloden_battlefield_today">Culloden battlefield today</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Culloden battlefield today">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Culloden_Battlefield_Memorial_Cairn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Culloden_Battlefield_Memorial_Cairn.jpg/220px-Culloden_Battlefield_Memorial_Cairn.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Culloden_Battlefield_Memorial_Cairn.jpg/330px-Culloden_Battlefield_Memorial_Cairn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Culloden_Battlefield_Memorial_Cairn.jpg/440px-Culloden_Battlefield_Memorial_Cairn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Culloden_Battlefield_Memorial_Cairn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Memorial <a href="/wiki/Cairn" title="Cairn">cairn</a> erected in 1881.<sup id="cite_ref-nts.org.uk-Cairn_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nts.org.uk-Cairn-69">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Today, a <a href="/wiki/Visitor_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Visitor centre">visitor centre</a> is located near the site of the battle. This centre was first opened in December 2007, with the intention of preserving the battlefield in a condition similar to how it was on 16 April 1746.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> One difference is that it currently is covered in shrubs and <a href="/wiki/Ericaceae" title="Ericaceae">heather</a>; during the 18th century, however, the area was used as common <a href="/wiki/Grazing" title="Grazing">grazing</a> ground, mainly for tenants of the Culloden estate.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-9192_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-9192-71">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Those visiting can walk the site by way of footpaths on the ground and can also enjoy a view from above on a raised platform.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Possibly the most recognisable feature of the battlefield today is the 20 feet (6.1&#160;m) tall memorial <a href="/wiki/Cairn" title="Cairn">cairn</a>, erected by Duncan Forbes in 1881.<sup id="cite_ref-nts.org.uk-Cairn_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nts.org.uk-Cairn-69">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In the same year Forbes also erected headstones to mark the mass graves of the clans.<sup id="cite_ref-graves_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-graves-73">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Thatched_roof" class="mw-redirect" title="Thatched roof">thatched roofed</a> farmhouse of Leanach which stands today dates from about 1760; however, it stands on the same location as the <a href="/wiki/Sod" title="Sod">turf</a>-walled cottage that probably served as a <a href="/wiki/Field_hospital" title="Field hospital">field hospital</a> for government troops following the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-9192_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-9192-71">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> A stone, known as "The English Stone", is situated west of the Old Leanach cottage and is said to mark the burial place of the government dead.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> West of this site lies another stone, erected by Forbes, marking the place where the body of Alexander McGillivray of Dunmaglass was found after the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> A stone lies on the eastern side of the battlefield that is supposed to mark the spot where Cumberland directed the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The battlefield has been <a href="/wiki/Inventory_of_Historic_Battlefields_in_Scotland" title="Inventory of Historic Battlefields in Scotland">inventoried</a> and protected by <a href="/wiki/Historic_Scotland" title="Historic Scotland">Historic Scotland</a> under the Historic Environment (Amendment) Act 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Culloden_grave_(road_and_three_graves).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Culloden_grave_%28road_and_three_graves%29.jpg/220px-Culloden_grave_%28road_and_three_graves%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Culloden_grave_%28road_and_three_graves%29.jpg/330px-Culloden_grave_%28road_and_three_graves%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Culloden_grave_%28road_and_three_graves%29.jpg/440px-Culloden_grave_%28road_and_three_graves%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1202" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Culloden_grave_(road_and_three_graves).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 1881, Duncan Forbes erected the headstones that mark the mass graves of fallen Jacobite soldiers. They lie on either side of an early 19th-century road which runs through the battlefield.<sup id="cite_ref-graves_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-graves-73">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Since 2001, the site of the battle has undergone <a href="/wiki/Topographic" class="mw-redirect" title="Topographic">topographic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geophysical" class="mw-redirect" title="Geophysical">geophysical</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Metal_detector" title="Metal detector">metal detector</a> surveys in addition to <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_excavation" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeological excavation">archaeological excavations</a>. Interesting finds have been made in the areas where the fiercest fighting occurred on the government left wing, particularly where Barrell's and Dejean's regiments stood. For example, pistol balls and pieces of shattered muskets have been uncovered here which indicate close quarters fighting, as pistols were only used at close range and the musket pieces appear to have been smashed by pistol/musket balls or heavy broadswords. Finds of musket balls appear to mirror the lines of men who stood and fought. Some balls appear to have been dropped without being fired, some missed their targets, and others are distorted from hitting human bodies. In some cases it may be possible to identify whether the Jacobites or government soldiers fired certain rounds, because the Jacobite forces are known to have used a large quantity of French muskets which fired a slightly smaller <a href="/wiki/Caliber" title="Caliber">calibre</a> shot than that of the British Army's <i><a href="/wiki/Brown_Bess" title="Brown Bess">Brown Bess</a></i>. Analysis of the finds confirms that the Jacobites used muskets in greater numbers than has traditionally been thought. Not far from where the hand-to-hand fighting took place, fragments of mortar shells have been found.<sup id="cite_ref-gla.ac.uk-culloden_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gla.ac.uk-culloden-79">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Though Forbes's headstones mark the graves of the Jacobites, the location of the graves of about sixty government soldiers is unknown. The recent discovery of a 1752 silver <i><a href="/wiki/Thaler" title="Thaler">Thaler</a></i>, from the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Mecklenburg-Schwerin" title="Duchy of Mecklenburg-Schwerin">Duchy of Mecklenburg-Schwerin</a>, may however lead archaeologists to these graves. A geophysical survey, directly beneath the spot where the coin was found, seems to indicate the existence of a large rectangular burial pit. It is thought possible that the coin was dropped by a soldier who once served on the continent, while he visited the graves of his fallen comrades.<sup id="cite_ref-gla.ac.uk-culloden_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gla.ac.uk-culloden-79">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
The National Trust of Scotland is currently attempting to restore Culloden Moor, as closely as possible, to the state it was in during the Battle of Culloden Moor. They are also attempting to expand the land under its care to ensure the full battlefield is protected under the NTS. Another goal is to restore Leannach Cottage and allow visitors to once again tour the interior.
</p>
<h2><span id="Order_of_battle:_Culloden.2C_16_April_1746"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Order_of_battle:_Culloden,_16_April_1746">Order of battle: Culloden, 16 April 1746</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Order of battle: Culloden, 16 April 1746">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jacobite_army_2">Jacobite army</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Jacobite army">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Stuart" title="Charles Edward Stuart">Charles Edward Stuart</a><br />
Colonel John William Sullivan
</p>

The Master of Lovat's battalion missed the battle by several hours.</small><sup id="cite_ref-Reid2006-Lovat1-p20_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid2006-Lovat1-p20-83">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>

Led by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_McGillivray_of_Dunmaglass&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alexander McGillivray of Dunmaglass (page does not exist)">Alexander McGillivray of Dunmaglass</a>. Lost most of its officers at Culloden.</small>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2"><b>Farquharson of Monaltrie's Battalion</b>: 150 men.
</td>
<td><small>Consisted of mostly Highlanders but not all. Described by James Logie as "dressed in highland clothes mostly".</small><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;note 8&#93;</a></sup> <small>Included a party of <a href="/wiki/Clan_Gregor" title="Clan Gregor">MacGregors</a>.</small><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;note 9&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2"><b>Maclachlans and Macleans</b>: ~ 200 men.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><small>Commanded by Lachlan <a href="/wiki/Clan_Maclachlan" title="Clan Maclachlan">Maclachlan</a> of Castle Lachlan and Maclean of Drimmin (who served as Lt Col). The unit campaigned as part of the Athole Brigade, though fought at Culloden for the first time as a stand-alone unit.</small><sup id="cite_ref-Reid2006-p15-26_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid2006-p15-26-90">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2"><b>Chisholms of Strathglass</b>: ~ 80 men.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><small>This very small unit was led by Roderick Og <a href="/wiki/Clan_Chisholm" title="Clan Chisholm">Chisholm</a>. Suffered very heavy casualties at Culloden.</small><sup id="cite_ref-Reid2006-p15-26_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid2006-p15-26-90">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="3"><b><a href="/wiki/James_Drummond,_3rd_Duke_of_Perth" title="James Drummond, 3rd Duke of Perth">Duke of Perth</a>'s Division</b>.
</td>
<td colspan="2"><b>MacDonald of Keppoch's Regiment</b>. 200 men.
</td>
<td><small>Commanded by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Macdonald,_17th_of_Keppoch" title="Alexander Macdonald, 17th of Keppoch">Alexander MacDonald of Keppoch</a>. This small regiment consisted of <a href="/wiki/Clan_MacDonald_of_Keppoch" title="Clan MacDonald of Keppoch">MacDonalds of Keppoch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clan_MacDonald_of_Glencoe" class="mw-redirect" title="Clan MacDonald of Glencoe">MacDonalds of Glencoe</a>,</small><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;note 10&#93;</a></sup> <small><a href="/wiki/Clan_Mackinnon" title="Clan Mackinnon">Mackinnons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clan_Gregor" title="Clan Gregor">MacGregors</a>.</small><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;note 11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reid2006-p15-26_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid2006-p15-26-90">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2"><b>MacDonald of Clanranald's Regiment</b>: 200 men.
</td>
<td><small>Commanded by MacDonald of Clanranald, younger, who was wounded during the battle. Disbanded at Fort Augustus about 18 April 1746.</small><sup id="cite_ref-Reid2006-p15-26_90-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid2006-p15-26-90">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2"><b>MacDonnell of Glengarry's Regiment</b>: 500 men.
</td>
<td><small>Commanded by Donald MacDonnell of Lochgarry. This regiment included a unit of Grants of Glenmoriston and Glen Urquhart.</small><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;note 12&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="8"><b><a href="/wiki/John_Roy_Stuart" class="mw-redirect" title="John Roy Stuart">John Roy Stuart</a>'s Division</b> (reserve)
</td>
<td rowspan="2"><b>Lord Lewis Gordon's Regiment</b>
</td>
<td><b>John Gordon of Avochie's Battalion</b>: 300 men.
</td>
<td><small>Commanded by John Gordon of Avochie.</small><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;note 13&#93;</a></sup>

<td colspan="2"><b>The Highland Battalion</b>: ~ 300 rank and file.

<td><small>The Highland Battalion consisted of eight companies of soldiers, some regular and some militia.<sup id="cite_ref-HighlandBrigade_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HighlandBrigade-103">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Four of these companies were from the <a href="/wiki/Campbell_of_Argyll_Militia" title="Campbell of Argyll Militia">Campbell of Argyll Militia</a>, three of these companies were from <a href="/wiki/Loudon%27s_Highlanders" title="Loudon&#39;s Highlanders">Loudon's 64th Highland Regiment</a> and one company was from the <a href="/wiki/42nd_Regiment_of_Foot" title="42nd Regiment of Foot">43rd (Black Watch) Highland Regiment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HighlandBrigade_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HighlandBrigade-103">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The battalion was commanded by Lt Col <a href="/wiki/John_Campbell,_5th_Duke_of_Argyll" title="John Campbell, 5th Duke of Argyll">John Campbell, 5th Duke of Argyll</a> of the 64th Highlanders.<sup id="cite_ref-HighlandBrigade_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HighlandBrigade-103">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> There was also one non-regimented <a href="/wiki/Independent_Highland_Companies" title="Independent Highland Companies">Independent Highland Company</a> (militia) present at the battle that had been raised by <a href="/wiki/William_Sutherland,_17th_Earl_of_Sutherland" title="William Sutherland, 17th Earl of Sutherland">William Sutherland, 17th Earl of Sutherland</a>, but it was kept in reserve.<sup id="cite_ref-Simpson_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson-104">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Parliament_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parliament-105">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></small>

<p><small>See the following reference for source of tables</small><sup id="cite_ref-British&amp;Jacobite-note1_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-British&amp;Jacobite-note1-106">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Of the 16 British infantry battalions, 11 were English, 4 were Scottish (3 Lowland + 1 Highland), and 1 Irish battalion.</li>
<li>Of the 3 British battalions of horse (dragoons), 2 were English and 1 was Scottish.</li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Battle_of_Culloden_in_art">The Battle of Culloden in art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: The Battle of Culloden in art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Culloden_woodcut_painting_1746.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Battle_of_Culloden_woodcut_painting_1746.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Culloden_woodcut_painting_1746.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Battle_of_Culloden_woodcut_painting_1746.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Culloden_woodcut_painting_1746.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Battle_of_Culloden_woodcut_painting_1746.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Culloden_woodcut_painting_1746.jpg 2x" data-file-width="699" data-file-height="403" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Culloden_woodcut_painting_1746.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Woodcut painting by <a href="/wiki/David_Morier" title="David Morier">David Morier</a> of the Battle of Culloden first published just six months after the battle in October 1746</div></div></div>
<ul><li><i>An Incident in the Rebellion of 1745</i> (as shown in the info box at the top of this page), by <a href="/wiki/David_Morier" title="David Morier">David Morier</a>, often known as "The Battle of Culloden", is the best-known portrayal of the battle, and the best-known of Morier's works. It depicts the attack of the Highlanders against Barrell's Regiment, and is based on sketches made by Morier in the immediate aftermath of the battle.</li>
<li>David Morier in fact made two paintings depicting the battle, the second (pictured right) is a coloured woodcut painting that shows a plan of the battlefield.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Augustin_Heckel" title="Augustin Heckel">Augustin Heckel</a>'</b>s <i>The Battle of Culloden</i> (1746; reprinted 1797) is held by the <a href="/wiki/National_Galleries_of_Scotland" title="National Galleries of Scotland">National Galleries of Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Culloden_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Culloden-113">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Battle of Culloden and consequent imprisonment and execution of the Jacobite prisoners of war is depicted in the song <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=88j_FfA6KkI">"Tam kde teče řeka Flee"</a> ("Where the Big Water Fleet flows") by the Czech Celtic-rock band <a href="https://cs.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hakka_Muggies" class="extiw" title="cs:Hakka Muggies">Hakka Muggies</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Sumo_(band)" title="Sumo (band)">Sumo</a></b> the Argentine band Sumo made a song titled <i>Crua Chan</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> chronicling the development of the battle. The work was composed by Italian-Scottish <a href="/wiki/Luca_Prodan" title="Luca Prodan">Luca Prodan</a>, bandleader; he had knowledge of the battle in his student years in <a href="/wiki/Gordonstoun" title="Gordonstoun">Gordonstoun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>.</li>
<li>Frank Watson Wood, (1862–1953). Although he was better known as a Naval artist who mainly painted in water colours Frank Watson Wood painted The Highland Charge at the Battle of Culloden in oil. Frank Watson Wood exhibited at Royal Scotland Academy, The Royal society of painters in water Colours and The Royal Academy.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Battle_of_Culloden_in_fiction">The Battle of Culloden in fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: The Battle of Culloden in fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Culloden_Cairn_at_Knoydart,_Nova_Scotia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Culloden_Cairn_at_Knoydart%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/220px-Culloden_Cairn_at_Knoydart%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Culloden_Cairn_at_Knoydart%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/330px-Culloden_Cairn_at_Knoydart%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Culloden_Cairn_at_Knoydart%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/440px-Culloden_Cairn_at_Knoydart%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2748" data-file-height="3664" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Culloden_Cairn_at_Knoydart,_Nova_Scotia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Culloden Memorial Cairn, <a href="/wiki/Knoydart,_Nova_Scotia" title="Knoydart, Nova Scotia">Knoydart, Nova Scotia</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li>The Battle of Culloden is an important episode in <a href="/wiki/D._K._Broster" title="D. K. Broster">D. K. Broster</a>'s <i>The Flight of the Heron</i> (1925), the first volume of her <i>Jacobite Trilogy</i>, which has been made into a TV serial twice: by Scottish Television in 1968 as eight episodes, and by the BBC in 1976.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Naomi_Mitchison" title="Naomi Mitchison">Naomi Mitchison</a>'s novel <i>The Bull Calves</i> (1947) deals with Culloden and its aftermath.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Culloden_(film)" title="Culloden (film)">Culloden</a></i> (1964), a <a href="/wiki/BBC_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="BBC TV">BBC TV</a> <a href="/wiki/Docudrama" title="Docudrama">docudrama</a> written and directed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Watkins" title="Peter Watkins">Peter Watkins</a>, depicts the battle in the style of 20th-century television reporting.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Dragonfly_in_Amber" title="Dragonfly in Amber">Dragonfly in Amber</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Diana_Gabaldon" title="Diana Gabaldon">Diana Gabaldon</a> (1992, London) is a detailed fictional tale, based on historical sources, of the Scots, High, and Lowlanders, mostly the Highlanders within Clan Fraser. It has the element of <a href="/wiki/Time_travel" title="Time travel">time travel</a>, with the 20th Century protagonist knowing how the battle would turn out and was still – once transported to the 18th century – caught up in the foredoomed struggle.</li>
<li>Basis for the STARZ series <i><a href="/wiki/Outlander_(TV_series)" title="Outlander (TV series)">Outlander</a></i>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Highlanders_(Doctor_Who)" title="The Highlanders (Doctor Who)">The Highlanders</a></i> (1966–67) is a serial in the BBC science fiction television series <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">Doctor Who</a></i>. The time-traveller known as <a href="/wiki/Second_Doctor" title="Second Doctor">the Doctor</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Companion_(Doctor_Who)" title="Companion (Doctor Who)">companions</a> <a href="/wiki/Polly_(Doctor_Who)" title="Polly (Doctor Who)">Polly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Jackson_(Doctor_Who)" title="Ben Jackson (Doctor Who)">Ben</a> arrive in the <a href="/wiki/TARDIS" title="TARDIS">TARDIS</a> in 1746, hours after the Battle of Culloden. The story introduces the character of <a href="/wiki/Jamie_McCrimmon" title="Jamie McCrimmon">Jamie McCrimmon</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Chasing_the_Deer" title="Chasing the Deer">Chasing the Deer</a></i> (1994) is a cinematic dramatisation of the events leading up to the battle, starring <a href="/wiki/Brian_Blessed" title="Brian Blessed">Brian Blessed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fish_(singer)" title="Fish (singer)">Fish</a></li>
<li><i>Drummossie Moor – Jack Cameron, The Irish Brigade and the battle of Culloden</i> is a historical novel<i> </i>by Ian Colquhoun (Arima/Swirl, 2008) which tells the story of the battle and the preceding days from the point of view of the Franco-Irish regulars or 'Piquets' who covered the Jacobite retreat.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Harold_Coyle" title="Harold Coyle">Harold Coyle</a>'s novel <i>Savage Wilderness</i>, the opening chapter deals with the protagonist's service battle of Culloden.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Culloden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Colonel John William Sullivan wrote, "All was confused&#160;... such a chiefe of a tribe had sixty men, another thiry, another twenty, more or lesse; they would not mix nor seperat, &amp; wou'd have double officers, yt is two Captns &amp; two Lts, to each Compagny, strong or weak&#160;... but by little, were brought into a certain regulation".<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">An unknown British Army corporal's description of the charge into the government's left wing: "When we saw them coming towards us in great Haste and Fury, we fired at about 50&#160;Yards Distance, which made Hundreds fall, we fired at about 50&#160;Yards Distance, which made Hundreds fall; notwithstanding which, they were so numerous, that they still advanced, and were almost upon us before we had loaden again. We immediately gave them another full Fire and the Front Rank charged their Bayonets Breast high, and the Center and Rear Ranks kept up a continual Firing, which, in half an Hour's Time, routed their whole Army. Only Barrel's Regiment and ours was engaged, the Rebels designing to break or flank us but our Fire was so hot, most of us having discharged nine Shot each, that they were disappointed".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">James Johnstone, a member of Glengarry's Regiment wrote that the ground was "covered with water which reached halfway up the leg".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Cumberland wrote of the Macdonalds: "They came running on in their wild manner, and upon the right where I had place myself, imagining the greatest push would be there, they came down there several times within a hundred yards of our men, firing their pistols and brandishing their swords, but the Royal Scots and Pulteneys hardly took their fire-locks from their shoulders, so that after those faint attempts they made off; and the little squadrons on our right were sent to pursue them".<sup id="cite_ref-Roberts_2002,_p._173_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts_2002,_p._173-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-56">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Cumberland wrote: "A captain and fifty foot to march directly and visit all the cottages in the neighbourhood of the field of battle, and search for rebels. The officers and men will take notice that the public orders of the rebels yesterday was to give us no quarter".<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-59">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A Highland Jacobite officer wrote: "We were likewise forbid in the attack to make use of firearms, but only of sword, dirk and bayonet, to cutt the tent strings, and pull down the poles, and where observed a swelling or bulge in the falen tent, there to strick and push vigorously".<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-63">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Out of 27 officers of the English "Manchester Regiment": one died in prison; one was acquitted; one was pardoned; two were released for giving evidence; four escaped; two were banished; three were transported; and eleven were executed. The sergeants of the regiment suffered worse, with seven out of ten hanged. At least seven privates were executed, some no doubt died in prison, and most of the rest were transported to the colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Farquharson of Monaltrie's Battalion is sometimes referred to as the "Mar" battalion of Lord <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Gordon" title="Lewis Gordon">Lewis Gordon</a>'s Regiment, and raised in Braemar and upper Deeside by Francis Farquharson of Monaltrie.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This party of MacGregors were attached to Farquharson of Monaltrie's battalion of Lord Lewis Gordon's Regiment. They were commanded by MacGregor of Inverenzie.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2006-22_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2006-22-87">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-93"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-93">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Attached to the MacDonald of Keppoch's Regiment was MacDonald of Glencoe's Regiment. It joined the Jacobite army on 27 August 1745 and served the rest of the campaign attached to MacDonald of Keppoch's Regiment. This was a very small unit, of no more than 120 men, and was commanded by Alexander MacDonald of Glencoe. It surrendered to General Campbell on 12 May 1746 and had suffered 52 killed, 36 wounded. Instead of a regimental standard, the regiment is said to have marched behind a bunch of heather attached to a pike.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-94"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-94">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">MacGregors serving in MacDonald of Keppoch's Regiment were commanded by John MacGregor of Glengyle.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2006-22_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2006-22-87">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Grant of Glenmoriston's Battalion was a very small unit of ~ 80–100 men, from Glenmoriston and Glen Urquhart. The unit was commanded by Maj Patrick Grant of Glenmoriston and Alexander Grant, younger of Shewglie. About 30 men from this unit were killed at Culloden, though both Glenmoriston and Shewglie, younger escaped. Almost all of the 87 of the men from this unit who surrendered on 4 May were transported.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2006-19_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2006-19-95">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-97">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sometimes referred to as the "Strathbogie" Battalion of Lord Lewis Gordon's Regiment. Many of the 300 men were highlanders, though most feudal levies and mercenaries – <i>not</i> clansmen. An intelligence report of 11 December 1745 stated that of the 300 men, "only 100 have joined; mostly herds and hiremen from about Strathbogie and unaquainted with the use of arms; many are pressed and intend to desert&#160;...".<sup id="cite_ref-SR2006-19_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2006-19-95">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-99"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-99">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The unit was recruited in Edinburgh, by Stuart who was a captain in the <i>Royal Écossais</i> at the time. For a time the unit included some former members of the British Army. At the battle it eventually stood in the front, next to the Stewarts of Appin.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-101">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A composite regiment formed in March 1746 by combining the dismounted <a href="/wiki/Lord_Kilmarnock" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Kilmarnock">Lord Kilmarnock</a>'s Horse, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lord_Pisligo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lord Pisligo (page does not exist)">Lord Pisligo</a>'s Horse, and James Crichton of Auchingoul's Regiment, as well as forced recruits from Aberdeenshire courtesy of Lady Erroll (mother-in-law to Lord Kilmarnock).<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-102">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">At least two companies of MacGregors, commanded by James Mor Drummond, served in the Duke of Perth's Regiment.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2006-22_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2006-22-87">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-110">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed the 48th Foot in 1748.<sup id="cite_ref-SR2002-note_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR2002-note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
